ND State 158-95-16-9-2MBH - Well Evaluation
INTRODUCTION
The Liberty Resources Management Company, LLC. ND State 158-95-16-9-2MBH [SW SW
Section 16, T158N, R95W] is located approximately 7.3 miles north of Tioga in Williams
County, North Dakota. The subject well is designed as a double-section horizontal Middle
Bakken well within McGregor Field, situated along the western flank of the Nesson anticline of
the Williston Basin (Figure 1). A curve would be kicked off in the Lodgepole and landed within
the Middle Bakken. Directional drilling and geo-steering techniques would then be used to
maintain maximum exposure to the target zone over the course of one approximately 9,830' long
lateral drilled to the north (0.55º).
OFFSET CONTROL
Three offset wells were used as primary controls while drilling the ND State 158-95-16-9-2MBH
(Figure 1). Geological data from nearby offset wells were used to determine a prognosis of
formation tops. These wells include:
· The Liberty Resources Management Company, LLC ND State 158-95-16-9-2TFH
[SW SW Section 16, T158N, R95W] which is located approximately 35' west of the
subject well on the same pad.
· The Amerada Hess Corporation NDCA 16-23X [NE SW Section 16, T158N, R95W]
which is located approximately 0.23 miles north-northeast of the subject well.
· The Liberty Resources Management Company, LLC ND State 158-95-16-9-10TFH
[SW SW Section 16, T158N, R95W] which is located approximately 70' west of the
subject well.
The vicinity of these wells to the subject well's surface location made them ideal for generating a
well-rounded prognosis of formation tops. In addition to the aforementioned offsets, the Morris
Gohrick 1-A [NW NW Section 9, T158N, R95W] well was used for structure control
geosteering of the lateral.
Figure 1. GIS map of well location, existing wells, offset wells and fields (NDIC, GIS
map server, 2014).
GEOLOGICAL EVALUATION
Lithology
The top of the Middle Bakken was logged at 9,561' TVD (-7,076' MSL). It consists primarily of
a medium to light gray to gray brown colored silty sandstone exhibiting trace to occasional
amounts of spotty light brown oil staining and possible intergranular porosity (Figure 2). The
targeted silty sandstone has an interbedded white to off-white lime packstone facies high in
section.
Figure 2. Cuttings from the Middle Bakken (Theresa
O'Reilly, Sunburst Well-site Geologist).
Curve Landing
Geological data in the form of drilling parameters, drill cuttings and MWD gamma ray were used
to determine marker and formation tops during the vertical hole and curve build sections of the
well. Tops were correlated to the offset wells and associated isopach thicknesses to the relevant
prospect in order to determine an appropriate landing target. A landing target of 9,584' TVD
was calculated while drilling the Lodgepole and no adjustments were made to the landing target
after reaching the Lodgepole "X" marker. An intermediate casing point of 9,900' MD (9,590.02
TVD) was designated at an inclination of 86.04°.
Geosteering
The ideal target zone was defined as a 20' interval set 9' below the base of the Upper Bakken
Shale and 28' above the Lower Bakken shale (Figure 3). The most useful signature for steering
purposes was a clean, cool gamma marker reading 20-40 API, underlain by a hot spike reading
75-95 API. This gamma pattern was representative of the lower boundary of the lime packstone
directly above the ideal target, and about midway between the top and base of the target interval.
Offset wells indicated that the Middle Bakken well would have a gross apparent down-dip of
approximately 0.03° from initial entry to total depth. While drilling the ND State 158-95-16-9-
2MBH the Middle Bakken dropped an estimated 5.20' over 9,998', resulting in an actual gross
apparent dip of 0.03° down.
The bottom-hole location is estimated to be 10,029.65' north and 74.99' east of surface location
or approximately 221.95' FNL and 1,203.99' FWL NW NW Section 9, T158N, R95W. Geo-
steering techniques exposed 72% of the uncased borehole to the 20' ideal Middle Bakken target.
The well reached a total depth of 19,730' MD on November 7, 2014.

Gas Monitoring
Background gas (C1-C4) fluctuated between 90 and 400 units on average during different
sections of the lateral (Figure 4). Sections of elevated gas measurements were recorded between
14,225' and approximately 14,900' MD and from 18,000' through 19,000' MD. During both
intervals, the wellbore was near the base of the packstone or within the packstone. The initial
elevated gas interval occurred where dip turned over from an up-dip to a down-dip, or at the crest
of the apparent anticline. The highest gas value recorded was a connection gas of 2,643 units at
14,429' MD. The entire ideal target zone was observed to contain relatively moderate gas
concentrations and trace to rare oil staining. Drill fluid was diverted through the gas buster
starting at 12,664' MD.

Sunburst Well-site Geologist).
Hydrogen sulfide (H2S) was also detected during lateral drilling starting at 9,920' MD.
Concentrations of H2S ranged from 0 to 100 parts-per-million and a strong odor was emitting on
location at various times. Higher readings of H2S are likely a result of the specific H2S sensor
reading other component gases.
SUMMARY
1)
The Liberty Resources Management Company, LLC. ND State 158-95-16-9-2MBH was
spud on September 23, 2014 and reached total depth in 18 drilling days on November 7,
2014.
2)
Samples from the Middle Bakken target consisted primarily of medium to light gray to
gray brown colored silty sandstone with possible intergranular porosity and trace to
occasional amounts of spotty light brown oil staining. The top half of the target interval
was included a unit of white to off-white lime packstone with trace even oil staining.
Samples yielded moderate fluorescent cuts.
3)
Moderate gas shows (C1-C4) were present throughout the well. On average background
gas ranged between 90 and 400 units. Sections of elevated gas measurements were
recorded within or near the packstone facies from 14,225' through about 14,900' MD and
from 18,000' through 19,000' MD. The highest gas value recorded was a connection gas
of 2,643 units at 14,429' MD.
4)
The ND State 158-95-16-9-2MBH awaits completion operations to maximize its
production potential.
Respectfully submitted,
Theresa O'Reilly
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
November 7, 2014

LITHOLOGY
ND State 158-95-16-9-2MBH
Rig crews caught 30' sample intervals from 7,200' to 19,730' MD (TD). Formation tops and lithologic markers
have been inserted into the sample descriptions below for reference. Sample descriptions begin in the Mississippian
Otter Formation. Samples were examined wet and dry under a binocular microscope. Sample fluorescence cuts are
masked by invert mud through intermediate casing. Quantifiers in order of abundance are trace, rare, occasional,
common and abundant.
Drilling in the Otter Formation [Mississippian, Big Snowy Group]
7,200-7,230 SHALE: dark gray, occasional medium gray, firm, blocky, earthy texture
7,230-7,260 SHALE: dark gray, occasional medium gray, firm, blocky, earthy texture
Kibbey [Mississippian Big Snowy Group]
7,262' MD / 7,256' TVD (-4,771')
7,260-7,290 SHALE: dark gray, occasional medium gray, firm, blocky, earthy texture; SILTSTONE: light pink, tan,
light gray-gray brown, SANDSTONE: light pink, orange tan, very fine grained, sub angular, poorly sorted, friable,
earthy texture
7,290-7,320 SHALE: dark gray, occasional medium gray, firm, blocky, earthy texture; SILTSTONE: light pink, tan,
light gray-gray brown, SANDSTONE: light pink, orange tan, very fine grained, sub angular, poorly sorted, friable,
earthy texture
7,320-7,350 SHALE: dark gray, occasional medium gray, firm, blocky, earthy texture; SILTSTONE: light pink, tan,
light gray-gray brown, SANDSTONE: light pink, orange tan, very fine grained, sub angular, poorly sorted, friable,
earthy texture
7,350-7,380 SHALE: dark gray, occasional medium gray, firm, blocky, earthy texture; SILTSTONE: light pink, tan,
light gray-gray brown, SANDSTONE: light pink, orange tan, very fine grained, sub angular, poorly sorted, friable,
earthy texture
Kibbey Lime [Mississippian, Big Snowy Group]
7,409' MD / 7,403' TVD (-4,918')
7,380-7,410 SHALE: dark gray, occasional medium gray, firm, blocky, earthy texture; SILTSTONE: light pink, tan,
light gray-gray brown, SANDSTONE: light pink, orange tan, very fine grained, sub angular, poorly sorted, friable,
earthy texture
7,410-7,440 LIMESTONE: mudstone, cream-light gray, microcrystalline, blocky, hard-firm, crystalline texture
7,440-7,470 SILTSTONE: light orange, light medium orange brown, blocky, soft, occasionally friable, rare firm,
slightly calcareous, sandy in part, no visible porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: light cream-brown, off white,
cryptocrystalline, soft, earthy texture
7,470-7,500 SILTSTONE: light orange, light medium orange brown, blocky, soft, occasionally friable, rare firm,
slightly calcareous, sandy in part, no visible porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: light cream-brown, off white,
cryptocrystalline, soft, earthy texture
7,500-7,530 SILTSTONE: light orange, light medium orange brown, blocky, soft, occasionally friable, rare firm,
slightly calcareous, sandy in part, no visible porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: light cream-brown, off white,
cryptocrystalline, soft, earthy texture
Charles Salt [Mississippian, Madison Group]
7,556' MD / 7,549' TVD (-5,064')

LIMESTONE: cream-light gray, mudstone, microcrystalline, blocky, firm-hard, crystalline texture

Dear Terry:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24759, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The approval
is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than the 200' setback
from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the 2560 acre spacing unit
consisting of Sections 9, 16, 21 & 28 T158N-R95W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Be advised the 20401 JV-P NDCA 5 well is within 449 feet of the proposed
wellbore for the ND STATE 158-95-16-9-2MBH well. Precautions must be taken while designing the frac job
for the ND STATE 158-95-16-9-2MBH well as to not adversely affect the 20401 JV-P NDCA 5 well. Be
advised the 20401 JV-P PATRICIA 14-9 well is within 296 feet of the proposed wellbore for the ND STATE
158-95-16-9-2MBH well. Precautions must be taken while designing the frac job for the ND STATE 158-95-
16-9-2MBH well as to not adversely affect the 20401 JV-P PATRICIA 14-9 well. Effective June 1, 2014, a
covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site
beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back
whenever filtration operations are conducted. LIBERTY RES MNGMT CO must contact NDIC Field
Inspector Tom Delling at 701-770-8660 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling
and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent
pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are
prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill
cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The
proposed directional plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal
coordinate from the well head is: 10051 N.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be
waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information necessary to
evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other information that
would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit, the
applicant should retain the permit.

Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card .The permit fee has been received. It is requested that

p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours
or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor shall
file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must be
submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the
directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the operation of the
director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe document, with a
certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or
when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours,
and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the
plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well
bore, and (3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic
cement evaluation log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior
to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format)
copy and one digital LAS (log ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or
attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov
Thank you for your cooperation.

RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director

3. Casing and cementing will be done to protect potentially productive
hydrocarbons, fresh water zones, abnormal pressure zones,
and prospectively valuable mineral deposits.
A. Casing head: 9 5/8" x 11" 5M multi-bowl w/ flange 22" below GL,Initial BOPE test to 5000 psi. unless 9 5/8" is pre set then SOW
Tubing head 11" 5M x 7 1/16" 10M. BOPE test to 5000 psi before drilling out 7" casing shoe.
B. Operators minimum specifications for pressure control equipment are shown on the attached BOP
schematic. After running surface casing and prior to drilling out, blind rams, pipe rams, manifold,
upper and lower kelly cock and safety valve will be pressure tested to 5000 psi. Hydril will be tested
to 2500 psi. Thereafter, the BOPE will be checked daily for mechanical operations and will be noted
in the IADC drilling reports. Before and after running the intermediate casing the BOPE will be tested
in the same manner. BOP will be tested at both high 5000 psi and low pressure to 250 psi.
Gas Buster will be fully rigged up and tested for fluid integrity, using anti-freeze solution
prior to drilling out surface casing.

10. Deviation & MWD Surveys

Surface to KOP: Maintain Inclination less than 3 degrees. Adjust KOP as necessary.
Directional Surveys every 90' from surface to KOP.
MWD Surveys every 30' from KOP To landing 7" 90 ft surveys through horizontal.
GammaRay - Will be logged from KOP, through build section, and through lateral section.

D. Other Drilling Considerations & Lessons Learned:
1. Gas Buster- Not to be used for venting off flowline. Divert all flow to gas buster.
2. Lateral Drilling- Minimize DLS.
3. Salt Sections: Tight hole and stuck pipe may occur. Control drill +/-5' and back-ream
as necessary. Spot freshwater only if severely stuck.
4. Do not rotate PDC bit inside 7" casing while displacing well with kill weight fluids.
Ensure bit & motor are in open hole section.
5. Transfer OBM from storage tanks to rig tanks over the shaker screens.
6. CaCL Brine truck to location after running/cmt'g 7 inch csg. To be determined each well.

STATEMENT
According to NDAC Section 43-02-03-19.2 and as outlined in the NDIC letter dated
4/9/14, Liberty Resources Management Company, LLC plans to abide with the filtration
container requirement for oil and gas operations on their ND State multi-well pad
location (SW Section 16-T158N-R95W, Williams County, ND, which includes the
following wells:
ND State 158-95-16-9-10TFH
ND State 158-95-16-9-1TFH
ND State 158-95-16-9-2MBH
ND State 158-95-16-9-2TFH
ND State 158-95-21-28-1MBH
ND State 158-95-21-28-2MBH
ND State 158-95-21-28-2TFH

Suite 2050
Denver, CO 80202
(303) 749-5757

a. Anticipated date of first production.
January 5, 2015.
b. Anticipated oil and gas rates and duration. If well is on a multi-well pad, include total
for all wells being completed.
Anticipated Oil and Gas Rates and Duration: Well production rates estimated as 1000
bopd and 2 mmcfd initial production rate average for 30 days with oil rate declining at
80% thereafter.
Anticipated Oil and Gas Rates and Duration (Multi-Well Pad):
Total production rate for four wells on pad is 4000 BOPD and 8 mmcfd expected initial
production rate average for 30 days with oil rate declining at 80% thereafter .
5. Amount of gas applicant is currently flaring.
a. Statewide percentage of gas flared (total gas flared/total gas produced) for existing
wells producing from the Bakken petroleum system. Note industry target goals are to
reduce flaring to 26% by 9-1-14, 23% by 1-1-15, 15% by 1-1-16, and 10% by 9-1-20:
Statewide percentage of gas flared for existing Liberty operated wells in June 2014 was
9%.
b. Field wide percentage of gas flared:
Fieldwide (McGregor Field) percentage of gas flared for existing Liberty operated wells
in June 2014 was 6%.
Liberty Resources Management Company, LLC
Gas Capture Plan
July 22, 2014
6. Alternatives to flaring.
a. Explain specific alternate systems available for consideration:
We have evaluated alternative gas utilization schemes including gas fired power
generation and pad processing to separate gas liquids.
b. Detail expected flaring reductions if such plans are implemented:
Based upon our existing gas connections and proximity to gas gathering lines and the
Tioga Gas Plant, we do not require additional options for flaring reductions.
